LAO PD1R
PROVINCIAL GRID NETGRATION PROJECT
Terms of Reference for Feasibility Study for Nam Ngum Power Station Expansion
Background
1.        The Nam Ngum Hydropower Station is located on the Nam Ngum river
abot 80 km north of Vientiane. The existing facilities, having a total
capacity of 150 MW and an annual energy production of about 820 GWh, were
completed under three phases: Phase I, t.wo 15 MW units placed in commercial
operation in 1971; Phase II, two 40 MW units placed in commercial operation in
19'8; and Phase III, a 40 MW unit placed in commercial operation in 1984.
2.        The Nam Song and Nam Leuk hydropower schemes are located upstream of
the existing Nam Ngum reservoir.  The first scheme comprises diversion of part
of the flows of the Nam Song into the Nam Ngum reservoir while the second
comprises diversion of the flows of the Nam Leuk into the reservoir through a
power station on the Nam Xan. A prefeasibility study of these two projects
was completed in 1990 by the Beca Wdorley International (BWI) in association
with Lahmeyer International under a technical assistance grant by ADB.
Contract for the feasibility and design study of these two projects has been
signed recently between ADB and BWI/Latimeyer.
3.        To optimize the benefits of these schemes, the Nam Ngum Hydropower
Station is to be extended to utilize effectively the additional flows to be
diverted into the reservoir.
Scope of Work
4.        The scope of work comprises:  (a) a review of the development plans
of Nam Ngum Hydropower Station Extension included in the prefeasibility report
of Nam Son-Nam Leuk Hydropower Development Study (Attachment I); (b) optimiza-
tion of the installed capacity of Nam Ngum Extension taking into account of
the findings of the feasibility and design study for Nam Song-Nam Leuk
Development scheduled to be completed by late 1992; (c) detailed design of the
works; (d) an estimate of the cost of the works; (e) preparation of a project
implementation schedule; (f) an economic and financial analysis of the
project; (g) preparation of terms of reference for consulting services for
project implementation; and (h) preparation of project reports.



- 80 -
ANNEX 3.9
Page 2 of 3
Detailed Terms of Reference
5.        The consultant shall carry out:
(a) In addition to the following three alternatives examined in the
prefeasibility stage: (i) a'40 MW extension to the existing power
station, (ii) a 60 MW extension to the existing power station; and
(iii) a 2 x 40 MW installation in a new power station on the left
bank downstream of the existing power station, other alternative
should be studied by locating a new surface or underground power
station utilizing the diversion tunnel located on the right bank of
the dam..
(b) Optimization studies to establish the most economic installed
capacity of Nam Ngum Extension taking into consideration the
additional flows to be diverted into the Nam Ngum reservoir, the
optimal operation of the Nam Ngum power station, and the time-of-day
tariff agreement entered recently between EGAT and EDL.
Cc) A detail review of the construction methods proposed in the
prefeasibility study.
(d) Detailed design, preparation of drawings and specifications for the
components of the project including a schedule of quantities.
(e) Estimation of the cost of constructing the scheme including the
civil, mechanical and electrical works and provision of a cash flow
projection (for civil works the estimates will be built up from
labor, equipment and material inputs and be expressed as unit prices
applied to a schedule of quantities).
(f) Identification of contract packaging.
(g) Preparation of an implementation schedule and construction program
(the construction program shall be broken down into major item sof
works and shall give time requirements for completion of each task
taking into consideration the start time imposed by the implementa-
tion schedule and any seasonal constraints to construction).
(h) Economic and financial analysis of the project taking into account:
total costs including, construction, operation and maintenance; and
benefits from the sale of the additional energy generated at Nam
Ngum power station (the analysis shall calculate the economic and
financial rates of return and include sensitivity analyses for
variations in project costs, diverted flows and tariffs).
(i) Preparation of terms of reference for consulting services to prepare
tender documents for construction of the works, carryout tender
evaluation, supervise construction and commissioning of the works.



- 81 -
ANNEX 3.9
Page 3 of 3
(j) Preparation of the following reports (in addition to monthly
progress reports): Inception Report, Mid-Term Report, Draft Design
Report and Final Design Report.
Consultancy Inputs
6.        The study is expected to be carried out over nine month period and a
total of 45 manmonths of foreign consultancy inputs including expertise in
hydropower layout and design; hydropower construction; electrical/mechanical
design; cost estimate and power economics. EDL will provide the following
facilities to assist carrying out of the study:
(a) suitable counterpart staff;
(b) field assistance;
(c) office facilities including secretarial services; and
(d) vehicles including drivers.
Reports
7.        The following reports, all in the English language, will be
submittad by the consultants to the Government of the Lao PDR, EDL and the
Bank. The inception report, mid-term report, and the draft final report will
be reviewed and commented upon by the Government, EDL and the Association.
(a) Inception Report. This report will be submitted within four weeks
after commencement of services and will outline a detailed work
program and briefly describe the work steps proposed to fulfill the
terms of reference.
(b)  Mid-Term Report.  This report to be submitted at the end of month
three will recommend the most optional plant layout and installed
capacity.
(c) Draft Final Report. This report will detail the consultants'
findings and recommendations and will be submitted within seven and
one-half months from the commencement of the consultants' services.
(d) Final Report. This report will incorporate all revisions required
by the Government, EDL and the Association on the Draft Final Report
(within six weeks of submitting the same).

Assumptions to Financia Projections
Income Statement
(1)  Total Generation -- is derived in the table entitled "Sales and
Generation" (page 17).
(2) Losses -- are derived in the table entitled "Sales and
Generation" (page 17).
(3)  Energy Sold -- is derived in the table entitled "Sales and
Generation" (page 17).
(4)  Income from Electricity Sales -- is derived in the table
entitled "Derivation of Average Tariff" (page 6).
(5)  Other Income Exclusive of Sales -- is projected to increase by
12X per year.
(6)  Salaries and Allowances -- are derived in the table entitled
"Direct Cash Flow" (page 18).
(7)  Cost of Bulk Purchases -- is derived in the table entitled
"Direct Cash Flow" (page 18).
(8)  Other Cash Operating Expense -- are derived in the table
entitled "Direct Cash Flow" (page 18).
(9) Depreciation -- is derived in the table entitled "Fixed Asset
Formation" (page 11).
(10) Total Interest Payments -- are the sum of interest capitalized
and interest charged to operations.
(11) Interest Capitalized is derived in the schedule entitled
"Borrowings Summary" (page 13).
(12) Interest Charged to Operations -- is derived in the schedule
entitled "Borrowings Summary* (page 13).
(13) Government Tax -- is set at 25Z of Total Operating Expenses plus
Interest charged to Operations.
(14) Dividend -- is darived in the schedule entitled "Dividends and
Reserves' (page 19).

Page 23 of 24
Flow of Funds
(15) Net Working Capital Increases -- exclude Cash and Liquidity
Requirements.
(16) Principal Repayments -- are derived in the schedule entitled

LAO PDR
PROVINCIAL GRD INTEGRATION PROJECT
Eecticdte du Laos
Action Program for Reduding Arrears from Government Agendes
1.          The aims of this  rogram are to:  (i) improve significantly the
collection of current billing; (ii) make arrangements to collect over time, a
significant part of the past arrears; and (iii) make arrangements to write
down that portion of past arrears that is considered uncollectible.
Elements of the Program
2.          Set up a system to simplify the offset of Government related
receivables against remittances to the Government. The ultimate objective is
tv lower the arrears to three months of turnover by April 1994. To ensure
that the reduction of Government and Government related receivables does not
have an excessive fiscal impact, the aggregate reduction will be accomplished
in steps. The first group of offsets would aim to teduce turnover to seven
months, the second set to five months, and the third to the ultimate target of
three months, where the Government and EdL would strive to maintain it
thereafter.
3.          A written agreement between the Ministry of Finance and EdL will
define the conditions upon which the compensation can be made. It is proposed
to:
(i) deduct the debts of the Government agencies directly from their
budget allocation. This adjustment should take place yearly in
April; and
(ii) deduct the debts of the Government agencies directly from the
taxes to be remitted to the Government. This second adjustment
should take place yearly in October.
4.          According to the terms of the above agreement:
(i)   At the end of March 1993, EdL will prepare and send to the
Ministry of Finance, the list of the Government and Government
related agencies with receivables of over 3 months together with
the amount that should be deducted from their budget allocation.
The adjustment expected in April 1993 would be Kips 223 millions;
(ii) At the end of September 1993, EdL will prepare and send to the
Ministry of Finance, the list of the Government and Government
related agencies with receivables of over three months together
with the amount that will be deducted directly from the next



- 116 -                            ANNEX 4.2
Page 2 of 3
remittances. The adjustment expected in October 1993 would be Kips
273 millions; and
(iii)   At the end of April 1994, EdL will prepatre and send to the
Ministry of Finance, the list of the Government and Government
related agencies with receivables of over 3 months with the amount
that should be deducted from their budget allocation. The
adjustment expected in April 1994 would be Kips 302 millions.
Maintaining the above system in operation beyond April 1994 is essential as it
can be expected that some Government or Government related agencies will still
experience some difficulties in paying their energy bills regularly. However,
the future adjustments based on the above principles are likely to be well
under the first three ones.
5.          Automatically, EdL will accrue interest on overdue payments for
the bills unpaid after three months. The rate used by the banking system to
remunerate the saving accounts in local currency will be utilized.  EdL will
compute and show on the bills to delinquent Government and Government related
agencies the amounts owing for more than three months and separately the
amount of interest thereon. The accrued interest will be considered part and
parcel of energy debt.
6.          Ask agencies with receivables outstanding of more than three
months and which are not directly under government control, to pay a deposit
of about 2 to 3 months of consumption. If necessary, to highlight the
seriousness of the issue, EdL may need to disconnect several of these non
governmental defaulters. Where defaulters with deposits accrue receivables
that exceed three months, EdL will be authorized to interrupt their
electricity supply, provided a notice was sent to the customer 8 days before,
and solutions to reach an agreement had failed. The deposit would then be
used to compensate for the accrued debts and the cost of disconnection. Prior
to reconnection, the non Governmental agency will have to pay a new deposit,
settle the remaining arrears, if any, and pay the cost of reconnection.
7.          For consumer agencies that are small and weak and have limited
ability to generate cash, develop a system aimed at limiting their power
consumption by installing a small circuit breaker close to the meter. This
will prevent them from installing new electrical equipment. The resultant
limitation of power will be discontinued as soon as the agency establishes a
record of regular payments.
